< Review>
Great little place for wine and small plates/charcuterie. One of the servers (maybe manager or owner) was really friendly and informative, the others did what they had to or were asked to do. Small parking lot in front and a good amount of street parking nearby. Worth a visit, but if you're starving, make sure to fill up a bit before visiting.< /Review>

<review>I absolutely adore Barsha. I only discovered it recently and have been back multiple times. The atmosphere is intimate and cozy for a small group wine tasting. They offer excellent dips, cheeses, and small bites to accompany the wine. You can order a wine flight or by the glass depending on the occasion. If you're just looking to pick up a great cheese and wine for a party, the staff is great at making recommendations. We had a friend's small birthday get together here the other week and it was a blast! Highly recommend it.

Edit: pro tip! They will give you an all red or all white flight if you ask for it!< /review>< Date>

< Text>
Went last night with a friend after yoga class.  The waiter gave us two seating options.  One spot was sitting side by side facing an art wall, so we chose option 2, on a high table where we could sit on the corner and face each other.  Another waiter came over and moved us saying a party had reserved it.  So we moved to the less desirable seat.  We were there for an hour and no one ended up sitting at the table we originally wanted.  The same waiter took our order and we only got part of our order.  I don't know if he thought we were under dressed (yoga attire) or if it was that there was only 2 of us but he was only concerned about the bigger parties in the room.  The owner came at the end and offered us the bruschetta on the house but we were done with our wine and ready to leave. Surprisingly, we got our check with nothing comped.  Disappointing experience.  Won't be going back.</Text>

<Review>My first thought on the first visit was "this place would KILL in the Manhattan Beach village" but now I love and appreciate it even more exactly because it's *NOT* in the village!

After driving past wondering about Barsha for so long I've been in several times now and realized quickly all the 5 star reviews are real. There's nothing not to love: the retail side is a surprisingly interesting and well-curated wine selection, with a lot of European, old-world, and esoteric stuff that you will absolutely NOT find anywhere else in the South Bay. Also some craft beers, outstanding whiskey and spirits section, quirky gifts, Riedel stemware, and killer cheeses and charcuterie to take home--which brings us the the "other" side of the room: the tasting and munchies bar.

The 4-selection wine flights, half glasses, and full glasses available are ALL great and change monthly.  The owner and chief pourer Adnen has fantastic taste and knowledge and chooses these carefully, and so far I've loved every single selection. But the munchies..... wow, not your everyday cheapo cheese and crackers. They surprised the hell out of me with the super high quality of cheeses, charcuterie, p√¢t√©s, homemade dips, and broiled warm baguette pieces drizzled liberally with Tunisian olive oil that makes me hungry just thinking about it.

But most importantly everyone is nice! The staff is super friendly which must be a reflection of Adnen and his wife Lenora. Adnen is probably going to be the warmest and most engaging owner you'll ever meet in ANY business. It's a great and laid back vibe and it just always feels good in there. Pop in soon and I'm sure you'll agree. 5 stars well earned!<//Review>< username>

I had been in pain for a couple weeks every time I ate. The pain would go away, but as anyone who has had tooth pain knows, any is not a good sign. I knew I had a cavity and that if I didn‚Äôt get it filled, I would need a root canal.
I have no medical insurance, let alone dental insurance.
I called the office and the receptionist (Barbara?) was super nice and very kind. They made me an appointment for the next day.
The office offered me a deal because I was paying in cash. They also told me that as a new patient, if I got my teeth cleaned and they looked over my whole mouth, I would be saving money. (Rather than just getting that painful spot looked at.)
Turns out I had two cavities, I got the painful one filled that day, and they made an appointment for the next month to fix the other cavity. I didn‚Äôt want to be totally numb.
I didn‚Äôt eat before I came in, and they offered me a snack, so I wouldn‚Äôt be  uncomfortable while they were working on my teeth.
I was injured by a dentist when I was younger and I had put off going to the dentist for years, out of fear.
This place is amazing. My dentist, Dr. Fnu Sabina, was super kind and explained exactly what she was going to do, she numbed me before even giving me the numbing shot. I didn‚Äôt have any pain at any point during the procedure.
The assistant and the dentist were amazing. I‚Äôm not afraid to go to this office.
I can‚Äôt even begin to tell you (whoever may be reading this) how grateful and elated I am to have a dentist I trust and look forward to seeing again.

<Rate>1<//Rate>< Text>
Staff here are just horribly rude. Two minutes after I and a group of friends walked a younger female employee rounded the same corner we just had, looking like she'd just run a marathon to catch up to us. She immediately accosted us, telling us to "not play" with the items we had casually picked up to look at, and asked us if we needed any help. We said we were fine - to which she replied with (I kid you not) "I'm sure you are", in the sassiest, most sarcastic tone I would think possible. She proceeded to follow our group around the store, making her presence overtly known by pretending to make sure all the display cabinets in our vicinity were locked by loudly banging on them. In general, she tried her best to make us as uncomfortable as possible to get us to leave. We were not loud, we were not rowdy, and we were not obnoxious. She obviously profiled us as young adults who weren't going to buy anything at the astronomical prices they charge, and was quick to pressure us out of the store - while completely ignoring a different group of women actually messing with the merchandise and being loud. The prices are sky-high, the antiques are completely mediocre, and the staff is RUDE BEYOND BELIEF! Frankly I'm not sure how they're still in business. If you want an actual selection of cool antiques at very decent prices, go to Granny's right next door. Whatever you do, don't step foot in here!</Text>

I've been a customer at Grandpa's Antique Mall for several years, and I think it's one of the best anywhere.  The atmosphere is clean and upbeat, with a great selection of antique, vintage and unusual items at good prices. The busy owners and staff always seem friendly and helpful.  In fact, I just heard that Grandpa's was voted the #2 Best Place To Buy Antiques in the region.  Grandpa's is absolutely a must-do stop for us when we're in Temecula, along with the wineries, shops, and Saturday morning Farmers Market.</text>

<rate>5</rate><Time>1562458160920</Time><pictures>None< /pictures><review>Went to Rim's Deli after finding it on Yelp. It was around 2pm and we had just got done fishing at the river all morning. We were hot, sweaty and hungry and I can tell you Rim's was the perfect spot to cure all that ailed me. I ordered the #3, a mortadella and provolone on a roll. The bread was fresh, mortadella sliced thin and piled high. It was delicious... especial after dousing it with a decent about of their Italian dressing and some yellow mustard. The soda I order, diet coke, was cold and hit the spot. But if you was a craft root beer or orange cream soda, they have plenty of those craft type sodas to choose from as well. The price was right for what you get and absolutely delicious. The sandwich chains don't have anything on Rim's. Oh one last thing, I was amazed by the staffs ability to stay busy. There was several young adults that kept busy the entire time, most notably when there were no customers to help. I really appreciated that as a retail manager myself. Anyway, if you in the mood for a good deli style sandwich and good service, give Rim's a try!< /review>< gmap_id>

<Review>Finally got a chance to visit Blade 1936.   Since hearing about their indoctrination into the Associazione Verace Pizza Napoletana (AVPN), which formally certifies their pizza as true, authentic Neapolitan pizza (one of only two in San Diego), I've been enthusiastically wanting to try out their pies.

We are surrounded by pizza joints - one near every corner it seems, and most of them are frankly sub-par.  Sure, even frozen pizza can taste okay, but you want the BEST.

I've learned that my favorite style of pizzas are either true deep-dish Chicago style, thin & greasy New York style (where you have to "fold" the pizza to eat it), OR Neapolitan style, where the outer crust is bubbly in some places, slightly burnt in other, crispy on the outside & fluffy on the inside all while being thin in the middle.  It's a very specific style of pizza.

Blade 1936, named after the 84 year old Blade-Tribune newspaper building they took over, is a great new addition to the Oceanside food scene.  They sit on Seagaze Avenue behind the large AMC multiplex downtown.  Parking wasn't too difficult to find, in fact we parked on the street right near the building.

They have a large patio dining section on the side of the place, but we chose to sit inside.  Seats are PADDED, too!  I can't tell you how important I think it is that restaurants make the decision to offer padded seats.  Save the metal chairs for breweries and other joints where you're drunk enough not to care how much your butt hurts.

We ordered some wine for the wife, a cocktail for me (the "Rumblepony" with Rum & Campari).  I actually wanted a beer instead, but wasn't impressed with the short selection of draft options (they also have a few bottles).  Most seemed to be IPAs.  There was a Peroni and Dolomiti on the bottle beer list, so keep that in mind.  Would like to see more draft options, or at least a better variety...

For an appetizer, we chose the "Polenta e Salsiccia" (Polenta with Fennel Sausage in a pink sauce).  I don't remember the last time I had polenta, but this dish makes me forget all the other times I've had it.  This was excellent.  The slight grittiness of the polenta matched well with the creamy pink sauce that was bustling with tasty bits of sausage.  We ate it all.

My wife ordered the Pappardelle Bolognese, and I had to try the Truffle Pizza (it was National Truffle Day afterall).  Both were excellent.  The pizza doesn't have any meat but it doesn't even need it.  The freshness of the arugula atop the puffy, slightly charred dough was magical with the slight flavor of truffle, mushrooms and mozzarella.

The pasta was excellent as well, and side note:  the leftovers tasted even better the next day.

Service was excellent.

I really liked the newspaper references located here and there inside.  At the end, even the receipt is served in a leather-bound tray that boasts a vintage, "newpapery" background.

If you check-in on Yelp, you'll get $5 off the bill.

Overall I really enjoyed Blade.  There are several flat-screen TVs around if you need to catch a game.  Some quiet Italian music in the background might be cool, however clich√©.  It's a smallish restaurant which probably seems that way due to social distancing.  I do wish the bar was a tad larger, but overall I was quite pleased with the food & service.  Looking forward to the next meal ;-)<//Review>< username>
Erich Cervantez< /username>

Little Italy experience in North County. Enjoy the ambiance and flavors of the most prestigious Little Italy restaurants in the comfort and pleasant views of North County. With the oceanside puer and other great spots within walking distance, Blade is definitely a must see when touring Oceanside.< /Text>

<text>Been here about 5 times since it opened and I want to give it a 5 star really badly (because food is very good, more on that below), however, everytime I go I am frustrated by the service. 3 out of the 5 times I have gone the server uses a little tablet to put in orders. They are ALWAYS so distracted putting in the order and trying to work the gadget that we have never had a personable or nice encounter with our server and 2 out of the 3 times they used this gadget our order was wrong because they pressed the wrong thing or were not listening because they were frustrated by the thing. You almost can always tell the server is upset or annoyed with having to use it. It is a big distraction!!!

The food though, that is good!!! Love the Prosciutto and Burrata appetizer (miss the basil with it though, it seems to have been switched out for arugula, but still so good!). The pizzas are always tasty!

Beer menu needs help! More beer options needed, local beer options would be best.

The building is really cool, love the atmosphere, especially the back room. The artwork (multicolored food pictures) in the main room and quite odd and don't really understand how they go with the place!

I am not a crazy nitpicky person, just love the new food places coming up in Oside and the service thing makes me sad. Oside is homey and feels like a small surf town and this service feels like downtown busy (not as friendly) San Diego service.<//text><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< Resp>

< review>
Four of us tried Blade the other night for the first time. We were very impressed. The food, service, prices, and the decor are all outstanding! Make a reservation if you can... it helps. I don't remember which pizza my friend got, but he wanted MEAT and he was quite happy with his. His wife got the papperdelle bolognese and I got the ravioli bolognese. My wife got the caprcciosa pizza (artichokes and black olives). I also had the Blade chopped salad. It was absolutely delicious! For $8, you won't find a nicer dinner salad. Lots of fresh ingredients with a light lemon dressing. I' a big fan of Italian food and Blade 1936 is a notch up from most of the others in the area. We've only been once, so I'll reserve further judgement til later. Loved it.< /review>

<Name>Rebecca Armendariz</Name><Time>1569691933562< /Time>< rate>
4</rate>
< Text>
Glad we got to try out Blade 1936 while we were in town this fall. First, I love the name and history behind this restaurant. My degree was in journalism and minor in history. Put me inside a building that used to house an old print newsroom and I'm in heaven! We showed up on a Friday night and were told it would be over an hour wait. Would have loved to have made a reservation, but when I called I was told they don't take reservations for parties less than six. (Looks like that may be changing soon. I saw an OpenTable plug-in on their site this morning.) Luckily two spots opened up at the bar and we grabbed them quickly. We ordered WAY too much. We just wanted to try a lot of the the food since we were only going to be in Oceanside another few days. I had the red sangria and Greg had the ginger margarita for cocktails. Both delicious. We ordered a bottle of the house cab with dinner. Totally worth it! Only $20 and a solid red. For apps we did the cauliflower/green beans and bison meatballs. They were both excellent. Great texture and flavor. For entrees we got the gnocchi funghi and seafood spaghetti. The gnocchi was a bit mushy and spaghetti seemed a tad firm. Both still had good flavor, though, and portions were perfect. We also ordered a margharita pizza to split (because you have to when at an Italian restaurant, right?!) and it did not disappoint! (UPDATE: I reheated my pizza on stovetop the following day and it was equally satisfying.) We were way too full for dessert, so ended our night there. I can't wait to try out this place again when we are back in a few months.</Text>

I can really tell interior has not been touched neither the engine compartment which is full of dust and dirt after the clean up service. I did not bother anymore to complain about this as this was very frustrating and too much on my part to keep going after them for a better overall service after all that had happened.

this is just my experience or opinion. Hope it helps you out there for your next car experience.<//Review>

< text>
This was a solid dinner and I would definitely go again. Most of the dishes were about $30, except for a large, 60 day aged ribeye ($67). Our waiter suggested it would be a good one to share so my wife and I went for it as our main entree.

The rest of the items we ordered were great, but our steak, which we ordered medium rare, was medium well at best. We couldn't taste anything special about it. The waiter finally came by after quite a while and asked how it was. I never send anything back but was very disappointed with the steak and brought up how overcooked it was. He immediately offered a new one and we took him up on it.

It was a bit of a wait and I felt a bit guilty since we had eaten at least half the other steak, but I'm so glad we did. The second steak was a bit on the rare side, but it was an amazing steak. I've never had a dry age steak with that much flavor (and a bit of funk at times). So, in the end it was a wonderful experience and we loved the steak.</text>

< text>
Great restaurant for a nice night out with friends. Plenty of options for plates to share with friends, as well as mains for yourself. Their list of carefully crafted cocktails (plus AWESOME and knowledgeable bartenders), varietals of wine,  solid selection of beers, and non-alcoholic options ensure all members of your dining party are happily watered as they await the delicious food to come.

Appetizers/shared items:
Shishito peppers: perfectly blistered with that tasty finishing maldon salt evenly salting the peppers (even the ones on the bottom). A must-have for sharing with the table.

Sourdough batard with whipped duck fat: Can't go wrong with fresh, hot bread with a savory duck fat spread on top

Poutine: Well balanced gravy (not too salty! Yay!),  cheese, fries ratio. Glad that we chose to share this between the 5 of us, giving each of us just enough to enjoy the dish without stuffing ourselves.

Black Pepper Cavatelli: Again, great for sharing so that none of us felt guilty for filling up on pasta prior to our mains

Mains:
Duck breast: I ordered mine medium rare and it came out wonderful. Very tender and flavorful, paired very well with the vegetables (loved the turnips)  and fruit (plum).

Dessert:
Black Pepper Pound Cake: Don't wrinkle your nose at this if you're unsure about the foie gras chantilly. The depth brought out by the extra fat  and subtle flavor of the foie gras goes well with the pound cake (I appreciate that it wasn't overly sweet), contrasting with the light plum sorbet.

Matcha Cheesecake: This matcha cheesecake was DELICIOUS, but the angostura bitters sorbet was what hit this dessert out of the park.</text>

< Text>
I've worked a block away from Salt House for the past two years and just stepped foot into it last week.  The restaurant is two levels with a bustling bar and open kitchen on the first level.  Dreamforce was going on at the time, so that may have impacted the amount of traffic but every table was full and there was a steady turnover.  Our waitress was fantastic but the service was slow getting our drinks.  I had the beet and burratta salad to start which was absolutely fantastic and the scallops entree which was equally impressive.  I finished my meal with a cup of really flavorful coffee and the seasonally appropriate pumpkin cheesecake.  We really enjoyed the food here and will definitely return.  Reservations are definitely needed!</Text>

< Review>
The four stars is definitely for the service!  My party hadn't arrived yet, and the hostess kept an eye on me until they arrived.  There were a lot of people coming in, mostly with reservations and I was afraid I wouldn't get a table because I didn't have one.  But she was so accommodating and I didn't wait long for a table.

The food was really good.  I ordered salmon with chanterelle mushrooms and fava beans.  I was hoping for a bigger portion, especially for the price, but it was nonetheless delicious.  And we ordered to desserts to share: the raspberry cream tart and the brown butter cream cheese pound cake.  The tart was had just the right amount of sweetness and tartness.  The pound cake wasn't served sliced.  They were cut into half-dollar size circles on top of whipped cream with scattered strawberries.  It was really good, and I'm glad it wasn't a bigger piece because it can tell it would be heavy.

The atmosphere was lively for a Monday night, and I like the industrial decor.  I'd like to come back and try the poutine!</Review>
